## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt represents the net force per unit mass. The acceleration typically depends on position (restoring force, possibly nonlinear), velocity (damping), and potentially time (external driving).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing + damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear + external periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 - x**2) (nonlinear damping depending on amplitude)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Coulomb-like damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (v**2)**0.5 (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic restoring + damping)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (combined nonlinearities)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium; even powers (x²) break symmetry
- Velocity-proportional damping (c*v) produces exponential amplitude decay; velocity-cubed damping (c*v³) produces algebraic decay
- Van der Pol-type terms v*(c - x²) create self-sustained oscillations via negative damping at small amplitudes and positive damping at large amplitudes
- Periodic driving terms cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicate forced oscillation; look for resonance when driving frequency matches natural frequency
- Position-velocity coupling terms like x*v or x²*v indicate energy-dependent nonlinear dissipation mechanisms
- Cubic restoring force x³ with same sign as linear term (hardening spring) vs opposite sign (softening spring) produces qualitatively different dynamics
- Absence of explicit time dependence in the acceleration formula indicates an autonomous (conservative or dissipative) system
- If acceleration depends only on x (not v or t), the system is conservative and energy is preserved along trajectories
